                  <hi rend="ital">He wrapped,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">inwrapped, himself with his garment;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">تَلَفَّفَ</foreign>: (S, O:) or <foreign lang="ar">اشتمل بِالثَّوْبِ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">he wrapped the garment around the whole of his body so that his arm,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">hand, did not come forth from it:</hi> (K:) or, as some say, <hi rend="ital">he wrapped himself with the garment, and threw</hi> [<hi rend="ital">a part of</hi>] <hi rend="ital">it upon his left side.</hi> (TA.)                   <hi rend="ital">A state of union</hi> or <hi rend="ital">composedness:</hi> and <hi rend="ital">a state of disunion</hi> or <hi rend="ital">discomposedness:</hi> thus having two contr. significations: (MF, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">a united,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">composed, state of the affairs,</hi> (S, Msb, TA,) and <hi rend="ital">of the number,</hi> (TA,) of a people, or company of men: (S, Msb, TA:) and <hi rend="ital">a disunited,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">discomposed, state of the affairs</hi> [&amp;c.] thereof.                      <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> A man <hi rend="ital">smitten,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">blown upon, by the</hi> [<hi rend="ital">north,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">northerly,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">wind called</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شَمَال</foreign>: (S, O:) and in like manner, a meadow, and a pool of water left by a torrent; (O;) or, applied to this last, <hi rend="ital">smitten by the wind thus called so as to become cool:</hi> (S:) and hence, with <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>, wine <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">cool to the taste;</hi> (S, O, TA; *) or wine <hi rend="ital">exposed to the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شَمَال</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">and so rendered cool and pleasant:</hi> (TA: see also <foreign lang="ar">شَمُولٌ</foreign>:) and fire <hi rend="ital">upon which the wind called the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شَمَال</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">has blown:</hi> (S, O:) and a night <hi rend="ital">cold, with</hi> [<hi rend="ital">wind that is called</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">شَمَال</foreign>. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence,] <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  One <hi rend="ital">whose natural dispositions are liked, approved,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">found pleasant:</hi> (K:) from [the same epithet applied to] water upon which the <foreign lang="ar">شَمَال</foreign> has blown, and which it has cooled: or, as ISd thinks, from <foreign lang="ar">شَمُولٌ</foreign> [q. v.]: (TA:) or <foreign lang="ar">مَشْمُولُ الخَلَائِقِ</foreign> a man <hi rend="ital">whose natural dispositions are commended;</hi> as being likened to wine that is commended: and also <hi rend="ital">whose natural dispositions are discommended;</hi> as though from <foreign lang="ar">الشَّمَالُ</foreign>, because they do not commend it when it disperses the clouds: (Har p. 285:) [for] <foreign lang="ar">أَخْلَاقٌ مَشْمُولَةٌ</foreign> [sometimes] means <hi rend="ital">discommended, evil, natural dispositions.</hi> (IAar, ISk, TA.) The saying of Aboo-Wejzeh, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">مَشْمُولَةُ الأُنْسِ مَجْنُوبٌ مَوَاعِدُهَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> is expl. by IAar as meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">Her familiarity passes away with the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شَمَال</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">and her promises pass away with the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">جَنُوب</foreign> [which is the opposite of the <foreign lang="ar">شَمَال</foreign>]: or, as some relate it, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">مَجْنُوبَةُ الأُنْسِ مَشْمُولٌ مَوَاعِدُهَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [meaning in like manner, as is said in the TA, on the authority of IAar, in art. <foreign lang="ar">جنب</foreign>: or,] accord. to ISk, meaning <hi rend="ital">her familiarity is commended,</hi> 
                  <pb n="1602"/> because the <foreign lang="ar">جنوب</foreign>, with rain, is desired for abundance of herbage; <hi rend="ital">and her promises are not commended.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">نَوًى مَشْمُولَةٌ</foreign>, a phrase used by Zuheyr, is expl. as meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">A tract,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">place, towards which one journeys,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">that separates friends;</hi> because the [wind called] <foreign lang="ar">شَمَال</foreign> disperses the clouds: (TA:) or it means <hi rend="ital">quickly</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">soon</hi>] <hi rend="ital">becoming exposed to view;</hi> (ISk, O, TA;) from the fact that when the wind called the <foreign lang="ar">شَمَال</foreign> blows the clouds, they delay not to become cleared away, and to depart: (O:) or, accord. to IAar, it means <foreign lang="ar">مَأْخُوذٌ بِهَا ذَاتُ الشِّمَالِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">in which the direction of the left hand is taken</hi>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  In the saying, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">حَمَلَتْ بِهِ فِى لَيْلَةٍ مَشْمُولَةٌ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> the meaning is, <foreign lang="ar">فَرِعَةٌ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">One in a state of fright became pregnant with him in a certain night</hi>]. (TA, referring to the phrase <foreign lang="ar">شَمْلٌ مِنْ جُنُونٍ</foreign>.)
